MAKE SURE THAT YOU CLEAN IT AFTER EVERY USE TO ENSURE LONGEVITY OF THE DIFFUSER. It's a good idea to clean it with vinegar once every two weeks -- empty it and clean it like normal, then dry it. Fill it halfway up to the fill line and add about 5 drops of vinegar. Then let it run for about five minutes (don't forget that it will smell like vinegar so diffuse in a well-ventilated place). Then dump out the vinegar and water and it'll be all super. Loving this little thing! I have used citrus oils in it, which I hear yes and no as to whether or not you're really supposed to, but I personally haven't had any damage to the unit. Again, just make sure you're cleaning it thoroughly after every use. :)

Surprisingly to me, there was very little circuitry going on inside. Just about 4 small circuit boards connected to each other. I found the source of the problem. When you want black out in a bedroom (in this case a nursery) that is a problem.<br />That should be a deal breaker if you want to use this to help you sleep.<br /><br />This second item of concern is that it doesn't handle citrus oils. All of my oil blends have a citrus oil in them. I use them anyway. So far no issues. but...<br /><br />The third item of contention is one common to almost all low-priced diffusers. You cannot hook it up to a timer because there is no 'auto-on' feature. After 15 minutes you can no longer smell the oils, thats normal. The receptors are 'fatigued'. Ideally oils should be diffused 15 minutes every hour. Most diffusers do not have a built-in timer to handle this. The workaround is that you can have an aftermarket timer. However, if you unplug a an item and plug it back in and it does not automatically re-start, you know a timer will not work on this item.
